href="http://wembleystadium.com">wembleystadium<wbr />.com</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Wembley Stadium</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> stadium in <a href="/wiki/Wembley" title="Wembley">Wembley</a>, London, England, which opened in 2007, on the site of the original <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)" title="Wembley Stadium (1923)">Wembley Stadium</a>, which was demolished from 2002\xe2\x80\x932003.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> The stadium hosts major football matches including home matches of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England national football team</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a>. The stadium is also the temporary home of <a href="/wiki/Premier_League" title="Premier League">Premier League</a> football club <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> until at least October 2018, while <a href="/wiki/White_Hart_Lane" title="White Hart Lane">White Hart Lane</a> is being demolished and their <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_Stadium" title="Tottenham Hotspur Stadium">new stadium</a> is being constructed.\n</p><p>Wembley Stadium is owned by the governing body of English football, <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a> (the FA), through its subsidiary Wembley National Stadium Ltd (WNSL). The FA headquarters are in the stadium. With 90,000 seats, it is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_British_stadiums_by_capacity" class="mw-redirect" title="List of British stadiums by capacity">largest stadium in the UK</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_stadia_by_capacity" class="mw-redirect" title="List of European stadia by capacity">the second-largest stadium in Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Designed by <a href="/wiki/Populous_(company)" title="Populous (company)">Populous</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foster_and_Partners" title="Foster and Partners">Foster and Partners</a>, the stadium is crowned by a 134-metre-high (440&#160;ft) Wembley Arch which serves aesthetically as a landmark across London and structurally with the arch supporting over 75% of the entire roof load.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> The stadium was built by Australian firm <a href="/wiki/Multiplex_(company)" title="Multiplex (company)">Multiplex</a> at a cost of \xc2\xa3798&#160;million (\xc2\xa31.09 billion today).<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DailyMailCost1_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyMailCost1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Contrary to popular belief,<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Wembley Stadium does not have a retractable roof which covers the playing surface. Two partially retractable roof structures over the east and west end of the stadium can be opened to allow sunlight and aid pitch growth.\n</p><p>In addition to England home games and the FA Cup final, the stadium also hosts other major games in English football, including the season-opening <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">League Cup</a> final, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">FA Cup semi-finals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Trophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Trophy">Football League Trophy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_play-offs" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League play-offs">Football League play-offs</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Trophy" title="FA Trophy">FA Trophy</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FA_Vase" title="FA Vase">FA Vase</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_League_(division)" title="National League (division)">National League play-offs</a>. A <a href="/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories" title="UEFA stadium categories">UEFA category four</a> stadium, Wembley hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">2011</a> and <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Finals</a>, and will host both the semi-finals and final of <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2020" title="UEFA Euro 2020">UEFA Euro 2020</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The stadium hosted the Gold medal matches at the <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Olympic Games football tournament</a>. The stadium also hosts <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> final, <a href="/wiki/NFL_International_Series" title="NFL International Series">NFL London Games</a> and music concerts.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" tocsection-11"><a href="#Firsts_at_the_new_Wembley_Stadium"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Firsts at the new Wembley Stadium</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Football"><span class="tocnumber">4.1</span> <span class="toctext">Football</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-13"><a href="#Tottenham_Hotspur"><span class="tocnumber">4.1.1</span> <span class="toctext">Tottenham Hotspur</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Rugby_league"><span class="tocnumber">4.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rugby league</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Rugby_union"><span class="tocnumber">4.3</span> <span class="toctext">Rugby union</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-16"><a href="#American_football"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">American football</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#Boxing"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">Boxing</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Transport_connections"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Transport connections</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-19"><a href="#Rail_and_Underground"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Rail and Underground</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-20"><a href="#Onsite_parking"><span class="tocnumber">5.2</span> <span class="toctext">Onsite parking</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-21"><a href="#Bus"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Bus</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-23"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-24"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stadium">Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG/220px-Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG/330px-Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG/440px-Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4502" data-file-height="3377" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley-STadion_2013.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley Stadium exterior</div></div></div>\n<p>Wembley was designed by architects <a href="/wiki/Foster_%2B_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="Foster + Partners">Foster + Partners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Populous_(company)" title="Populous (company)">Populous</a> (formerly HOK Sport) and with engineers Mott Stadium Consortium, who were a collection of three structural engineering consultants in the form of <a href="/wiki/Mott_MacDonald" title="Mott MacDonald">Mott MacDonald</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinclair_Knight_Merz" title="Sinclair Knight Merz">Sinclair Knight Merz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aurecon" title="Aurecon">Aurecon</a>. The design of the building services was carried out by <a href="/wiki/Mott_MacDonald" title="Mott MacDonald">Mott MacDonald</a>. The construction of the stadium was managed by Australian company <a href="/wiki/Multiplex_(company)" title="Multiplex (company)">Multiplex</a> and funded by <a href="/wiki/Sport_England" title="Sport England">Sport England</a>, WNSL (Wembley National Stadium Limited), <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Department_for_Culture_Media_and_Sport" class="mw-redirect" title="Department for Culture Media and Sport">Department for Culture Media and Sport</a> and the <a href="/wiki/London_Development_Agency" title="London Development Agency">London Development Agency</a>. It is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_megaprojects#Stadiums_and_sporting_venues" title="List of megaprojects">most expensive stadia</a> ever built at a cost of \xc2\xa3798&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-DailyMailCost1_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DailyMailCost1-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and has the largest roof-covered <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> in the world. <a href="/wiki/Nathaniel_Lichfield" title="Nathaniel Lichfield">Nathaniel Lichfield and Partners</a> was appointed to assist Wembley National Stadium Limited in preparing the scheme for a new stadium and to obtain planning and listed building permission for the development.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium,_illuminated.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/220px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/330px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg/440px-Wembley_Stadium%2C_illuminated.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="428" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium,_illuminated.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley illuminated</div></div></div>\n<p>The all-seater stadium is a bowl design with a capacity of 90,000, protected from the elements by a sliding roof that does not completely enclose it. It can also be adapted as an athletic stadium by erecting a temporary platform over the lowest tier of seating.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The stadium\'s signature feature is a circular section lattice arch of 7&#160;m (23&#160;ft) internal diameter with a 315&#160;m (1,033&#160;ft) span, erected some 22\xc2\xb0 off true, and rising to 133&#160;m (436&#160;ft).  It supports all the weight of the north roof and 60% of the weight of the retractable roof on the southern side.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The archway is the world\'s longest unsupported roof structure.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A "platform system" has been designed to convert the stadium for athletics use, but its use would decrease the stadium\'s capacity to approximately 60,000.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> No athletics events (track and field) have taken place at the stadium, and none are scheduled.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The conversion for athletics use was a condition of part of the lottery funding the stadium received, but to convert it would take weeks of work and cost millions of pounds.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction">Construction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Construction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg/220px-Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg/330px-Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg/440px-Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1758" data-file-height="1170" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_under_construction.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The stadium in its very early stages of construction c. August 2003</div></div></div>\n<p>The initial plan for the reconstruction of Wembley was for demolition to begin before Christmas 2000, and for the new stadium to be completed some time during 2003, but this work was delayed by a succession of financial and legal difficulties. In 2004, London Mayor <a href="/wiki/Ken_Livingstone" title="Ken Livingstone">Ken Livingstone</a> and Brent Council also announced wider plans for the <a href="/wiki/Regeneration_of_Wembley" class="mw-redirect" title="Regeneration of Wembley">regeneration of Wembley</a>, taking in the arena and the surrounding areas as well as the stadium, to be implemented over two or three decades. Demolition officially began on 30 September 2002, with the <a href="/wiki/Twin_Towers_(Wembley)" title="Twin Towers (Wembley)">Twin Towers</a> being dismantled in December 2002.\n</p><p>Delays to the construction project started as far back as 2003. In December 2003, the constructors of the arch, subcontractors <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Bridge_%26_Engineering_Company" title="Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Company">Cleveland Bridge &amp; Engineering Company</a> of <a href="/wiki/Darlington" title="Darlington">Darlington</a>, warned Multiplex about rising costs. Cleveland Bridge withdrew from the project and replaced by Dutch firm Hollandia with all the attendant problems of starting over. 2004 also saw errors, most notably a fatal accident involving carpenter Patrick O\'Sullivan for which construction firm PC Harrington Contractors were fined \xc2\xa3150,000 in relation to breaches of health and safety laws.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In October 2005, Sports Minister <a href="/wiki/Richard_Caborn" title="Richard Caborn">Richard Caborn</a> announced: "They say the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">Cup Final</a> will be there, barring six feet of snow or something like that". By November 2005, WNSL were still hopeful of a handover date of 31 March, in time for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FA_Cup_Final" title="2006 FA Cup Final">cup final</a> on 13 May. However, in December 2005, the builders admitted that there was a "material risk" that the stadium might not be ready in time for the final.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In February 2006 these worries were confirmed, with the FA moving the game to <a href="/wiki/Cardiff" title="Cardiff">Cardiff</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NewWembleyBuild.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/NewWembleyBuild.jpg/220px-NewWembleyBuild.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/NewWembleyBuild.jpg/330px-NewWembleyBuild.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/NewWembleyBuild.jpg/440px-NewWembleyBuild.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NewWembleyBuild.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction of the new Wembley, looking east, taken January 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>On 20 March 2006, a steel rafter in the roof of the new development fell by <span class="frac nowrap">1<span class="visualhide">&#160;</span><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>2</sub></span>&#160;ft (46&#160;cm), forcing 3,000 workers to evacuate the stadium and raising further doubts over the completion date which was already behind schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> On 23 March 2006, <a href="/wiki/Sanitary_sewer" title="Sanitary sewer">sewers</a> beneath the stadium buckled due to ground movement.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GMB_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="GMB Union">GMB Union</a> leader Steve Kelly said that the problem had been caused by the pipes not being properly laid, and that the repair would take months. Rumours circulated that the reason for the blockage was due to Multiplex failing to pay the contractors who laid the pipes who then filled in the pipes with concrete. A spokesman for developers <a href="/wiki/Multiplex_(company)" title="Multiplex (company)">Multiplex</a> said that they did not believe this would "have any impact on the completion of the stadium", which was then scheduled to be completed on 31 March 2006.\n</p><p>On 30 March 2006, the developers announced that Wembley Stadium would not be ready until 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> All competitions and concerts planned were to be moved to suitable locations. On 19 June 2006 it was announced that the turf had been laid. On 19 October 2006 it was announced that the venue was now set to open in early 2007 after the dispute between <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a> and Multiplex had finally been settled. WNSL was expected to pay around \xc2\xa336m to Multiplex, on top of the amount of the original fixed-price contract. The total cost of the project (including local transport infrastructure redevelopment and the cost of financing) was estimated to be \xc2\xa31&#160;billion.\n</p><p>For the new stadium the level of the pitch was lowered. During excavation of the new playing field, mechanical diggers unearthed a buried obstruction: the concrete foundations of <a href="/wiki/Watkin%27s_Tower" title="Watkin&#39;s Tower">Watkin\'s Tower</a>, a failed attempt to construct a rival to the <a href="/wiki/Eiffel_Tower" title="Eiffel Tower">Eiffel Tower</a> in London. Only the base of the tower was ever built before being abandoned and demolished in 1907; the site was later used as the location for the first Wembley Stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-delisle_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delisle-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Handover_and_opening">Handover and opening</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Handover and opening">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg/170px-Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg/255px-Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg/340px-Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg 2x" data-file-width="480" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bobby_Moore_Statue_outside_Wembley_Stadium_-_geograph.org.uk_-_602874.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Bobby_Moore,_Wembley" title="Statue of Bobby Moore, Wembley">Statue of Bobby Moore</a>, England\'s <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1966 FIFA World Cup">1966 FIFA World Cup</a> winning captain, stands outside the stadium entrance looking down <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Way" title="Olympic Way">Wembley Way</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The new stadium was completed and handed over to the FA on 9 March 2007. The official Wembley Stadium website had announced that the stadium would be open for public viewing for local residents of Brent on 3 March 2007, however this was delayed by two weeks and instead happened on 17 March.\n</p><p>While the stadium had hosted football matches since the handover in March, the stadium was officially opened on Saturday 19 May, with the staging of the <a href="/wiki/2007_FA_Cup_Final" title="2007 FA Cup Final">2007 FA Cup Final</a>. Eight days before that on Friday 11 May, the <a href="/wiki/Statue_of_Bobby_Moore,_Wembley" title="Statue of Bobby Moore, Wembley">statue of Bobby Moore</a> had been unveiled by <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Charlton" title="Bobby Charlton">Sir Bobby Charlton</a> outside the stadium entrance, as the "finishing touch" to the completion of the stadium. The twice life-size bronze statue, sculpted by <a href="/wiki/Philip_Jackson_(sculptor)" title="Philip Jackson (sculptor)">Philip Jackson</a>, depicts England\'s <a href="/wiki/1966_FIFA_World_Cup_Final" title="1966 FIFA World Cup Final">1966 World Cup winning</a> captain <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Moore" title="Bobby Moore">Bobby Moore</a>, looking down <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Way" class="mw-redirect" title="Wembley Way">Wembley Way</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-WNSL10May2007_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WNSL10May2007-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WNSL11May2007_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WNSL11May2007-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<ul><li>The stadium contains 2,618 toilets, more than any other venue in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The stadium has a circumference of 1&#160;km (0.62&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The bowl volume is listed at 1,139,100&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (1,489,900&#160;cu&#160;yd), somewhat smaller than the <a href="/wiki/Millennium_Stadium" title="Millennium Stadium">Millennium Stadium</a> in Cardiff, but with a greater <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-CONSTRUCTIONFACTS_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONSTRUCTIONFACTS-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>At its peak, there were more than 3,500 construction workers on site.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>4,000 separate piles form the foundations of the new stadium,<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> the deepest of which is 35&#160;m (115&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>There are 56&#160;km (35&#160;mi) of heavy-duty power cables in the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>90,000&#160;m<sup>3</sup> (120,000&#160;cu&#160;yd) of concrete and 23,000 tonnes (25,000 short tons) of steel were used in the construction of the new stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The total length of the escalators is 400 metres (<span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>&#8260;<sub>4</sub></span>&#160;mi).<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The arch has a cross-sectional diameter greater than that of a <a href="/wiki/Eurostar" title="Eurostar">cross-channel Eurostar train</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fascinating_Facts_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fascinating_Facts-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitch">Pitch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Pitch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_enggermatch.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wembley_enggermatch.jpg/220px-Wembley_enggermatch.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wembley_enggermatch.jpg/330px-Wembley_enggermatch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Wembley_enggermatch.jpg/440px-Wembley_enggermatch.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_enggermatch.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley Stadium pitch during <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> <a href="/wiki/Exhibition_match" class="mw-redirect" title="Exhibition match">friendly</a> against <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> in August 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>The pitch size, as lined for association football, is 115&#160;yd (105&#160;m) long by 75&#160;yd (69&#160;m) wide, slightly narrower than the old Wembley, as required by the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_stadium_categories" title="UEFA stadium categories">UEFA stadium categories</a> for a category four stadium, the top category.\n</p><p>Since the completion of the new Wembley, the pitch has come into disrepute since it was described as being "no good" and "not in the condition that Wembley used to be known for" by <a href="/wiki/Slaven_Bili%C4%87" title="Slaven Bili\xc4\x87">Slaven Bili\xc4\x87</a> before the game between <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> and the team he managed, <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> It was confirmed when the pitch was terribly cut up during the game, which was blamed by some<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> as the reason England did not qualify for <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2008" title="UEFA Euro 2008">UEFA Euro 2008</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> The Football Association admitted in April 2009 after the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_semi-finals" title="FA Cup semi-finals">FA Cup semi-finals</a> that improvements are needed to the Wembley pitch after criticism of the surface by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Ferguson" title="Alex Ferguson">Sir Alex Ferguson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ars%C3%A8ne_Wenger" title="Ars\xc3\xa8ne Wenger">Ars\xc3\xa8ne Wenger</a> and <a href="/wiki/David_Moyes" title="David Moyes">David Moyes</a>. The grass has been relaid ten times since the stadium re-opened in 2007 and was relaid again in the summer of 2009, ahead of the 2009 Community Shield.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2010, the surface was relaid for the 10th time since 2007, when the stadium was built. In April 2010, the pitch was again criticised following the <a href="/wiki/2009%E2%80%9310_FA_Cup" title="2009\xe2\x80\x9310 FA Cup">FA Cup semi-finals</a>, during which the players found it difficult to keep their footing and the surface cut up despite the dry conditions. The then <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur" class="mw-redirect" title="Tottenham Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</a> boss, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Redknapp" title="Harry Redknapp">Harry Redknapp</a> labelled it a "disgrace" after his side\'s semi-final defeat to <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> After the <a href="/wiki/2010_FA_Cup_Final" title="2010 FA Cup Final">2010 FA Cup Final</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> captain <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> said, "The pitch ruined the final. It\'s probably the worst pitch we\'ve played on all year. It was not good enough for a Wembley pitch."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> It was relaid with <a href="/wiki/Desso_GrassMaster" class="mw-redirect" title="Desso GrassMaster">Desso</a> semi-artificial pitch, ahead of the 2010 community shield game between <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_Football_Club" class="mw-redirect" title="Chelsea Football Club">Chelsea</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a>. <a href="/wiki/Michael_Owen" title="Michael Owen">Michael Owen</a>, who previously criticised the pitch for causing him injury, said that it was much improved.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Covering">Covering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Covering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg/220px-Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg/330px-Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg/440px-Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Arch_CloseUp.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Close-up of the arch</div></div></div>\n<p>The stadium roof has an area of 40,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (430,000&#160;sq&#160;ft), of which 13,722&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (147,700&#160;sq&#160;ft) is movable.<sup id="cite_ref-CONSTRUCTIONFACTS_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CONSTRUCTIONFACTS-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> The primary reason for the sliding roof was to avoid shading the pitch, as grass demands direct sunlight to grow effectively.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The sliding roof design minimises the shadow by having the roof pulled back on the east, west and south.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Angus Campbell, chief architect, also said that an aim was for the pitch to be in sunlight during the match between the beginning of May and the end of June, between 3&#160;pm and 5&#160;pm, which is when the FA and World Cups would be played. However, it was mentioned during live commentary of the FA Cup Final in 2007 that the pitch was in partial shade at the start at 3&#160;pm and also during the match.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_text_commentary_FA_Cup_Final_2007_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_text_commentary_FA_Cup_Final_2007-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The stadium roof rises to 52 metres (171&#160;ft) above the pitch and is supported by an arch rising 133&#160;m (436&#160;ft) above the level of the external concourse. With a span of 315&#160;m (1,033&#160;ft), the arch is the longest single-span roof structure in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures_37-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_Stadium_Facts_and_Figures-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Litigation">Litigation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Litigation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Australian firm Multiplex, which was the main contractor on Wembley Stadium, made significant losses on the project.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In an attempt to recoup some of those losses, the firm has initiated a number of legal cases against its sub-contractors and consultants.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The largest of these \xe2\x80\x93 the largest construction claim in UK legal history \xe2\x80\x93 was a claim for \xc2\xa3253&#160;million against the structural engineering consultants <a href="/wiki/Mott_MacDonald" title="Mott MacDonald">Mott MacDonald</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In preliminary hearings the two architecture practices which worked for Multiplex on the project were ordered to allow Multiplex access to their records in order for them to build a case. The practices, <a href="/wiki/Foster_%2B_Partners" class="mw-redirect" title="Foster + Partners">Foster + Partners</a> and <a href="/wiki/Populous_(architects)" class="mw-redirect" title="Populous (architects)">Populous</a>, estimated the costs of providing access and answering Multiplex\'s queries at \xc2\xa35&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The case was not due to be heard until January 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Mott MacDonald has issued a counter-claim for unpaid fees of \xc2\xa3250,000.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian.co.uk_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian.co.uk-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The dispute between Multiplex (now known as Brookfield) and Mott MacDonald was settled out of court in June 2010, the judge having warned that costs were likely to be more than \xc2\xa374&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Multiplex also took the original steel contractor, Cleveland Bridge, to court to claim up to \xc2\xa338&#160;million<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> compensation for costs resulting from Cleveland Bridge walking away from the job. Cleveland Bridge, in turn, claimed up to \xc2\xa315&#160;million from Multiplex. The case was finally resolved in September 2008 with Cleveland Bridge ordered to pay \xc2\xa36.1&#160;million in damages and 20% of Multiplex\'s costs after the court found Cleveland Bridge was in the wrong to walk off site. The judge criticised both sides for allowing the case to reach court, pointing out that total costs were \xc2\xa322&#160;million, including \xc2\xa31&#160;million for photocopying.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Multiplex\'s ultimate bill is estimated to be over \xc2\xa310&#160;million. In 2007, Multiplex also contested a claim from its concrete contractor, PC Harrington, that Multiplex owes \xc2\xa313.4&#160;million to PC Harrington.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bid_to_buy">Bid to buy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bid to buy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In April 2018, <a href="/wiki/Shahid_Khan" title="Shahid Khan">Shahid Khan</a>, the owner of <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham F.C.</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a>, put forward an offer to purchase Wembley Stadium from the FA. The deal included not only the purchase of the stadium, but also providing the FA full rights to keep control of the Club Wembley business.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> On 18 July 2018, a parliamentary select committee was held to discuss the possible sale, with evidence being given by former player, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Neville" title="Gary Neville">Gary Neville</a>, and Katrina Law of the <a href="/wiki/Football_Supporters%27_Federation" title="Football Supporters&#39; Federation">Football Supporters\' Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenants">Tenants</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tenants">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg/220px-Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg/330px-Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg/440px-Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1296" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_The_FA_Logo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of the governing body of English football, the FA, as displayed on the exterior of Wembley Stadium</div></div></div>\n<p>Given the ownership of the stadium by <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">the Football Association</a> (the governing body of English football), the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">English national football team</a> is a major user of Wembley. In 2007, the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Cup" title="EFL Cup">League Cup final</a> moved back to Wembley from Cardiff following the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_final" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Cup final">FA Cup final</a> and <a href="/wiki/FA_Community_Shield" title="FA Community Shield">FA Community Shield</a>.  Other showpiece football matches that were previously staged at Wembley, such as the <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League" title="English Football League">Football League</a> <a href="/wiki/English_Football_League_play-offs" title="English Football League play-offs">promotion play-offs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/EFL_Trophy" title="EFL Trophy">Football League Trophy</a> final, have returned to the stadium. In addition, the <a href="/wiki/National_League_(division)" title="National League (division)">Conference National</a> (now National League) play-off final is held at Wembley since 2007, and the <a href="/wiki/FA_Women%27s_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="FA Women&#39;s Cup">FA Women\'s Cup</a> final since 2015.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG/220px-Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG/330px-Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG/440px-Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_during_London_2012_Olympic_Games.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley Stadium during the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">London 2012 Olympic Games</a> <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">football tournament</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The new Wembley was a significant part of the plan for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> in London; the stadium was the site of several games in both the men\'s and women\'s <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Football at the 2012 Summer Olympics">football</a> tournaments, with the finals being held there.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The FA offices at Wembley Stadium, with social areas and boardroom, were designed by architects <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gebler_Tooth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Gebler Tooth (page does not exist)">Gebler Tooth</a> \xe2\x80\x93 who were also responsible for Team GB House at the London 2012 Olympics.\n</p><p>Additionally, the Rugby League <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> Final returned to Wembley Stadium in 2007, and the stadium also hosted both semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a>. Wembley was one of the 13 venues for the <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015 Rugby World Cup</a>.\n</p><p>Wembley has had a long association with <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a>.  A <a href="/wiki/United_States_Football_League" title="United States Football League">United States Football League</a> game was staged there in 1984,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> and between 1986 and 1993 the old Wembley Stadium hosted eight <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> exhibition games featuring 13 different NFL teams.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> Since the new Wembley Stadium opened in 2007 Wembley has hosted games during the NFL regular season.  As a result of this, <a href="/wiki/NFL_commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="NFL commissioner">NFL commissioner</a> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Goodell" title="Roger Goodell">Roger Goodell</a> stated in October 2009 that "he expects the NFL will start playing multiple regular-season games in Britain in the next few years, an expansion that could lead to putting <a href="/wiki/London_NFL_franchise" class="mw-redirect" title="London NFL franchise">a franchise in London</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> On 20 January 2012, the league announced that the <a href="/wiki/St._Louis_Rams" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Louis Rams">St. Louis Rams</a> would become a temporary tenant of Wembley Stadium, playing an annual game at the stadium every year from 2012 to 2014; part of the reason the Rams were chosen was the fact that the team is owned by <a href="/wiki/Stan_Kroenke" title="Stan Kroenke">Stan Kroenke</a>, who also is majority shareholder in a local Premier League team, <a href="/wiki/Arsenal_F.C." title="Arsenal F.C.">Arsenal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> However, the Rams later cancelled their 2013\xe2\x80\x932014 games,<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> leading to the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> becoming new temporary tenants and hosting games in London from 2013\xe2\x80\x932016.<sup id="cite_ref-NFL_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFL-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> This was later extended to 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-NFL_extend_Wembley_deal_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NFL_extend_Wembley_deal-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg/220px-Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg/330px-Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg/440px-Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6467" data-file-height="3201" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Race_of_Champions_2007_panorama.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley Stadium during the <a href="/wiki/2007_Race_of_Champions" title="2007 Race of Champions">2007 Race of Champions</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Race_of_Champions" title="Race of Champions">Race of Champions</a> staged their <a href="/wiki/2007_Race_of_Champions" title="2007 Race of Champions">2007</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Race_of_Champions" title="2008 Race of Champions">2008</a> events at the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> agreed with the operators (Wembley National Stadium Ltd) to use the stadium for all of their European fixtures during the <a href="/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2016\xe2\x80\x9317 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2016\xe2\x80\x9317 season</a>, before using the stadium for the entire <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2017\xe2\x80\x9318 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2017\xe2\x80\x9318 season</a>. They will also play their first four home games of the <a href="/wiki/2018%E2%80%9319_Premier_League" title="2018\xe2\x80\x9319 Premier League">2018\xe2\x80\x9319 season</a> at Wembley: against <a href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C." title="Fulham F.C.">Fulham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_F.C." title="Liverpool F.C.">Liverpool</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_F.C." title="Manchester City F.C.">Manchester City</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg/220px-LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg/330px-LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg/440px-LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LiveEarthWembleyStadium1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The stage at the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_London" title="Live Earth concert, London">Live Earth concert</a> held at Wembley on 7 July 2007.</div></div></div>\n<p>Besides football, Wembley can be configured to hold many other events, particularly major concerts but also private events like weddings and conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> This is an economic necessity given that the stadium ended up costing the FA much more than was originally projected. The regular covering of the pitch for concerts has led to the pitch being relaid often (see elsewhere in this article). Regular changes to the pitch mean that it never matches the quality of its surroundings, or of the pitch of the old Wembley in its later years. The first concert at the new stadium was given by <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> on 9 June 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a>, the last act to perform at the old Wembley, were scheduled to be the first artists to perform at the new Wembley but the late completion of the stadium saw the concerts relocated to the <a href="/wiki/National_Bowl" title="National Bowl">National Bowl</a> and the <a href="/wiki/KC_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="KC Stadium">KC Stadium</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/220px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/330px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG/440px-EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EltonJohnDianaConcert.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a> on piano at the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a> at Wembley on 1 July 2007, commemorating <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Princess Diana</a></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Muse_(band)" title="Muse (band)">Muse</a> became the first band to sell out the new stadium on 16 and 17 June 2007, and released a <a href="/wiki/HAARP_(album)" title="HAARP (album)">live DVD</a> of the performance.<sup id="cite_ref-Muse_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Muse-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Other acts to have performed at the stadium are <a href="/wiki/Metallica" title="Metallica">Metallica</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coldplay_(band)" class="mw-redirect" title="Coldplay (band)">Coldplay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)" title="Oasis (band)">Oasis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> and <a href="/wiki/AC/DC" title="AC/DC">AC/DC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Wembley hosted <a href="/wiki/Take_That_Present:_The_Circus_Live" class="mw-redirect" title="Take That Present: The Circus Live">Take That Present: The Circus Live</a> for four nights in summer 2009. The tour became the fastest selling tour in UK in history<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> before that record was broken by <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> two years later with their <a href="/wiki/Progress_Live" title="Progress Live">Progress Live</a> tour.\n</p><p>In the first week of July 2007, two large charity concerts were held at the new Wembley stadium, the <a href="/wiki/Concert_for_Diana" title="Concert for Diana">Concert for Diana</a>, a memorial concert to commemorate ten years since the <a href="/wiki/Death_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Death of Diana, Princess of Wales">death of Princess Diana</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_London" title="Live Earth concert, London">Live Earth</a>, a concert hosted at Wembley as part of the <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth" title="Live Earth">Live Earth Foundation</a>, committed to combating <a href="/wiki/Global_Warming" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Warming">climate change</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Take_That_Wembley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Take_That_Wembley.jpg/220px-Take_That_Wembley.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Take_That_Wembley.jpg/330px-Take_That_Wembley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Take_That_Wembley.jpg/440px-Take_That_Wembley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Take_That_Wembley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> concert in 2009</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FWT2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/FWT2.jpg/220px-FWT2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/FWT2.jpg/330px-FWT2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/FWT2.jpg/440px-FWT2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FWT2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The exterior of Wembley, following a <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyonc\xc3\xa9">Beyonc\xc3\xa9</a> concert during <a href="/wiki/The_Formation_World_Tour" title="The Formation World Tour">The Formation World Tour</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>95.8 <a href="/wiki/Capital_(radio_network)" title="Capital (radio network)">Capital FM</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Summertime_Ball" title="Summertime Ball">Summertime Ball</a>, which was previously hosted with 55,000 spectators at the <a href="/wiki/Emirates_Stadium" title="Emirates Stadium">Arsenal Emirates Stadium</a> and slightly less in <a href="/wiki/Hyde_Park,_London" title="Hyde Park, London">Hyde Park</a> (as <a href="/wiki/Party_in_the_Park" title="Party in the Park">Party in the Park</a>), was hosted at Wembley Stadium on 6 June 2010, and was headlined by <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a> and <a href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" class="mw-redirect" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>. The move to Wembley allowed many more fans to watch the annual music event which has previously lasted over 5 hours with more than 15 performers. It has since returned to the Stadium in 2011, 2012, 2013, 2014 and again in 2015 on 6 June. Rock band <a href="/wiki/Green_Day" title="Green Day">Green Day</a> continued their world tour, playing at Wembley on 19 June 2010. The gig was Green Day\'s biggest audience yet with over 90,000.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a> performed a song specially written for the Wembley Stadium: The Wembley Song. <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Flowers" title="Brandon Flowers">Brandon Flowers</a>, lead singer for The Killers said "We\'ve written a song for this joyous occasion." And proceeded to sing about some of Wembley\'s great moments, its history from the Twin Towers to present day arch.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Muse_(band)" title="Muse (band)">Muse</a> returned to Wembley Stadium on 10 and 11 September 2010 as part of their <a href="/wiki/The_Resistance_Tour" title="The Resistance Tour">Resistance Tour</a> to a sell-out crowd, having previously played there in June 2007. <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> played Wembley in 2008 during her <a href="/wiki/Sticky_and_Sweet_Tour" class="mw-redirect" title="Sticky and Sweet Tour">Sticky and Sweet Tour</a>, to a sold-out audience of 74,000.  The event has surpassed all gross revenue for a single concert at Wembley, grossing nearly US$12&#160;million.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Take_That" title="Take That">Take That</a> played a record breaking 8 nights at Wembley Stadium in summer 2011 on their <a href="/wiki/Progress_Live" title="Progress Live">Progress Live</a> tour, which has become the fastest and biggest selling tour in UK history.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_(night_2,_June_29th).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg/220px-Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg/330px-Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg/440px-Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_%28night_2%2C_June_29th%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4032" data-file-height="3024" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adele_Live_2017_-_The_FINALE_-_WEMBLEY_Stadium_-_LONDON_-_Make_You_Feel_My_Love_(night_2,_June_29th).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a> at Wembley Stadium in June 2017. Adele\'s concert on 28 June was attended by 98,000 fans, a stadium record for a UK music event.<sup id="cite_ref-Adele_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Adele-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>The Olympics meant that no concerts took place at Wembley in summer 2012, with other big shows taking place elsewhere. In summer 2013, there were seven big shows. The first act to perform at the venue was <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Springsteen" title="Bruce Springsteen">Bruce Springsteen</a>, who played his first show at the new stadium on 15 June. One week later, rock band <a href="/wiki/The_Killers" title="The Killers">The Killers</a> performed their biggest headline show at the venue on 22 June. <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Williams" title="Robbie Williams">Robbie Williams</a> then performed four solo concerts at the stadium on 29 and 30 June, and on 2 and 5 July after previously performing with Take That at the stadium in 2011. The summer\'s final show saw former Pink Floyd bass guitarist <a href="/wiki/Roger_Waters" title="Roger Waters">Roger Waters</a> play at the venue on 14 September as part of <a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Live_(concert_tour)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Wall Live (concert tour)">The Wall Live</a> tour. On 10\xe2\x80\x9312 July 2015, <a href="/wiki/Ed_Sheeran" title="Ed Sheeran">Ed Sheeran</a> performed three sold-out shows at Wembley as part of his world tour. The concert was documented and aired on 16 August 2015 on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>; the one-hour special <i>Ed Sheeran \xe2\x80\x93 Live at Wembley Stadium</i> also included behind-the-scenes footage.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a> completed her <a href="/wiki/Adele_Live_2016" title="Adele Live 2016">world tour</a> with two concerts, dubbed "The Finale", at Wembley on 28 and 29 June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-Wembley_2017_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wembley_2017-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup><a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a> played two shows as the first time at the Wembley Stadium for her <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift%27s_Reputation_Stadium_Tour" title="Taylor Swift&#39;s Reputation Stadium Tour">Reputation Stadium Tour</a> on 22 and 23 June 2018, <a href="/wiki/Camila_Cabello" title="Camila Cabello">Camila Cabello</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charli_XCX" title="Charli XCX">Charli XCX</a> was the opening act for the show.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Firsts_at_the_new_Wembley_Stadium">Firsts at the new Wembley Stadium</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Firsts at the new Wembley Stadium">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Flag.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Wembley_Flag.jpg/220px-Wembley_Flag.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Wembley_Flag.jpg/330px-Wembley_Flag.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Wembley_Flag.jpg/440px-Wembley_Flag.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Flag.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fans of the <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England football team</a> create the <a href="/wiki/St_George%27s_Cross" class="mw-redirect" title="St George&#39;s Cross">St George\'s Cross</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The first match at the stadium was a game played behind closed doors between Multiplex and Wembley Stadium staff.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The first game in front of spectators was between the Geoff Thomas Foundation Charity XI and the Wembley Sponsors Allstars on 17 March 2007. The Geoff Thomas Foundation Charity XI won 2\xe2\x80\x930 (scorers <a href="/wiki/Mark_Bright" title="Mark Bright">Mark Bright</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jordan" title="Simon Jordan">Simon Jordan</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The first official match involving professional players was <a href="/wiki/England_national_under-21_football_team" title="England national under-21 football team">England U21s</a> vs <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_under-21_football_team" title="Italy national under-21 football team">Italy U21s</a> on 24 March 2007, which finished 3\xe2\x80\x933. Official attendance was 55,700 (although all of the 60,000 tickets that were made available were sold in advance).<sup id="cite_ref-England_U21s_draw_Wembley_cracker_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_U21s_draw_Wembley_cracker-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The first player to score in a <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> sanctioned match was Italian striker <a href="/wiki/Giampaolo_Pazzini" title="Giampaolo Pazzini">Giampaolo Pazzini</a> after 28 seconds of the same game; he also scored the first <a href="/wiki/Hat-trick" title="Hat-trick">hat-trick</a> at Wembley. The first English player to score in a full-scale match was <a href="/wiki/David_Bentley" title="David Bentley">David Bentley</a> with a free kick in the same game.<sup id="cite_ref-England_U21s_draw_Wembley_cracker_90-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-England_U21s_draw_Wembley_cracker-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first club game, competitive game, and cup final held at the new Wembley took place on 12 May 2007 when <a href="/wiki/Kidderminster_Harriers_F.C." title="Kidderminster Harriers F.C.">Kidderminster Harriers</a> met <a href="/wiki/Stevenage_F.C." title="Stevenage F.C.">Stevenage Borough</a> in the <a href="/wiki/FA_Trophy" title="FA Trophy">FA Trophy</a> final.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Kidderminster striker <a href="/wiki/James_Constable" title="James Constable">James Constable</a> was the first player to score a goal in a final at the new Wembley. Kidderminster became the first team to play at both the old and new stadium.  Stevenage Borough were the first team to win a final at the new Wembley beating Kidderminster 3\xe2\x80\x932, despite trailing 2\xe2\x80\x930 at half time. The first players to play at both the old and new Wembley Stadiums were <a href="/wiki/Steve_Guppy" title="Steve Guppy">Steve Guppy</a> (for Stevenage Borough) and <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Kenna" title="Jeff Kenna">Jeff Kenna</a> (for Kidderminster Harriers).  Ex-<a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">England</a> international Guppy was the first player to win a final at both stadia (with <a href="/wiki/2000_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2000 Football League Cup Final">Leicester City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wycombe_Wanderers_F.C." title="Wycombe Wanderers F.C.">Wycombe Wanderers</a> and Stevenage). <a href="/wiki/Ronnie_Henry" title="Ronnie Henry">Ronnie Henry</a> was the first ever player to lift a competitive club trophy at the new Wembley.<sup id="cite_ref-Henry_the_first_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Henry_the_first-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlingcup.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Carlingcup.jpg/220px-Carlingcup.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Carlingcup.jpg/330px-Carlingcup.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Carlingcup.jpg/440px-Carlingcup.jpg 2x" data-file-width="604" data-file-height="453" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carlingcup.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C." title="Tottenham Hotspur F.C.">Tottenham Hotspur</a> celebrate winning the <a href="/wiki/Football_League_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League Cup">Football League Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a> in <a href="/wiki/2008_Football_League_Cup_Final" title="2008 Football League Cup Final">2008</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The first penalty save and first red card came in the <a href="/wiki/Conference_National" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference National">Conference National</a> playoff final between <a href="/wiki/Exeter_City_F.C." title="Exeter City F.C.">Exeter City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morecambe_F.C." title="Morecambe F.C.">Morecambe</a>. The penalty was saved by <a href="/wiki/Paul_Jones_(footballer,_born_1986)" title="Paul Jones (footballer, born 1986)">Paul Jones</a> of Exeter City from Morecambe striker <a href="/wiki/Wayne_Curtis" title="Wayne Curtis">Wayne Curtis</a>. The red card was given to <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Gill" title="Matthew Gill">Matthew Gill</a> of Exeter for a headbutt on <a href="/wiki/Craig_Stanley_(footballer)" title="Craig Stanley (footballer)">Craig Stanley</a> of Morecambe.<sup id="cite_ref-Exeter_1-2_Morecambe_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Exeter_1-2_Morecambe-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/Football_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Football League">Football League</a> teams to play at Wembley in a competitive fixture were <a href="/wiki/Bristol_Rovers_F.C." title="Bristol Rovers F.C.">Bristol Rovers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shrewsbury_Town_F.C." title="Shrewsbury Town F.C.">Shrewsbury Town</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2007_Football_League_Two_play-off_Final" title="2007 Football League Two play-off Final">2007 Football League Two play-off Final</a> on 26 May 2007. Shrewsbury Town became the first league team to score at Wembley via a <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Drummond" title="Stewart Drummond">Stewart Drummond</a> goal, they also the first league team to have a player sent off, in this case \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Marc_Tierney" title="Marc Tierney">Marc Tierney</a>\nBristol Rovers won the game 3\xe2\x80\x931 in front of 61,589 which was a stadium record until the Championship play-off final two days later when <a href="/wiki/Derby_County_F.C." title="Derby County F.C.">Derby County</a> beat <a href="/wiki/West_Bromwich_Albion_F.C." title="West Bromwich Albion F.C.">West Bromwich Albion</a> 1\xe2\x80\x930 to become the first team at the new stadium to win promotion to the FA Premier League.\n</p><p>The first <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">FA Cup Final</a> at the new Wembley (between <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United_F.C." title="Manchester United F.C.">Manchester United</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chelsea_F.C." title="Chelsea F.C.">Chelsea</a>) was on 19 May 2007, with a crowd attendance of 89,826.  Chelsea won 1\xe2\x80\x930 with a goal by <a href="/wiki/Didier_Drogba" title="Didier Drogba">Didier Drogba</a>, making him the first player to score in the FA Cup final at the new Wembley. Chelsea goalkeeper <a href="/wiki/Petr_%C4%8Cech" title="Petr \xc4\x8cech">Petr \xc4\x8cech</a> also became the first goalkeeper not to concede a goal in a competitive game at Wembley. Chelsea were the last winners of the cup final at the old Wembley and the first winners at the new.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/220px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/330px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg/440px-BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1836" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BVB-Fans_in_Wembley.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a> between <a href="/wiki/FC_Bayern_Munich" title="FC Bayern Munich">Bayern Munich</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borussia_Dortmund" title="Borussia Dortmund">Borussia Dortmund</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The first game involving the full <a href="/wiki/England_national_football_team" title="England national football team">English national team</a> was a friendly played on 1 June 2007, against <a href="/wiki/Brazil_national_football_team" title="Brazil national football team">Brazil</a>. The match saw <a href="/wiki/Captain_(association_football)" title="Captain (association football)">captain</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Terry" title="John Terry">John Terry</a> become the first England international goal scorer at the new stadium when he scored in the 68th minute. <a href="/wiki/Diego_Ribas_da_Cunha" class="mw-redirect" title="Diego Ribas da Cunha">Diego</a> became the first full international player to score for a visiting team when he scored in stoppage time, with the full-time result being a 1\xe2\x80\x931 draw.  The first competitive senior international was played on 8 September 2007 between England and <a href="/wiki/Israel_national_football_team" title="Israel national football team">Israel</a>. This game ended 3\xe2\x80\x930.  The first player to score international goals at both the old and new stadia was Michael Owen when he scored for England against Israel.  On 22 August <a href="/wiki/Germany_national_football_team" title="Germany national football team">Germany</a> beat England 2\xe2\x80\x931 to become the first team to beat them in the new Wembley Stadium. England\'s first competitive defeat at the new stadium was on 21 November 2007 when <a href="/wiki/Croatia_national_football_team" title="Croatia national football team">Croatia</a> won 3\xe2\x80\x932. This match cost England qualification to <a href="/wiki/Euro_2008" class="mw-redirect" title="Euro 2008">Euro 2008</a> and head coach <a href="/wiki/Steve_McClaren" title="Steve McClaren">Steve McClaren</a> his job.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Fullscore.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Fullscore.JPG/220px-Fullscore.JPG" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Fullscore.JPG/330px-Fullscore.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Fullscore.JPG/440px-Fullscore.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2144" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Fullscore.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a> fans celebrate winning the <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup" title="FA Cup">FA Cup</a> against <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2008_FA_Cup_Final" title="2008 FA Cup Final">2008 FA Cup Final</a>. The 89,974 attendance is the largest football attendance in the current Wembley\'s history</div></div></div>\n<p>On 17 May 2008, <a href="/wiki/FA_Cup_Final" title="FA Cup Final">the 127th FA Cup Final</a> was played (the second at the newly opened Wembley Stadium) between <a href="/wiki/Cardiff_City_F.C." title="Cardiff City F.C.">Cardiff City</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_F.C." title="Portsmouth F.C.">Portsmouth</a>.  The attendance of 89,874 fans is still a current record attendance for a competitive professional association football match in the current Wembley Stadium\'s history.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>  Portsmouth won the match 1-0 with a single 37th minute <a href="/wiki/Nwankwo_Kanu" title="Nwankwo Kanu">Nwankwo Kanu</a> goal.\n</p><p>Wembley Stadium hosted the <a href="/wiki/2011_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2011 UEFA Champions League Final">UEFA Champions League Final</a> on 28 May 2011 between <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">FC Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_United" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester United">Manchester United</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Wembley also hosted the <a href="/wiki/2013_UEFA_Champions_League_Final" title="2013 UEFA Champions League Final">2013 UEFA Champions League Final</a>, making it the second time in 3 years.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The event was held to mark the 150th anniversary of <a href="/wiki/The_Football_Association" title="The Football Association">The Football Association</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; overflow:hidden;
