width: -moz-min-content; width: -webkit-min-content; width: min-content; max-width: 100%;"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize overflowbugx" style="overflow: auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_panorama_3.jpg" class="image" title="A panorama of Wembley during the half time period of an England game"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b5/Wembley_panorama_3.jpg/1435px-Wembley_panorama_3.jpg" width="1435" height="230" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b5/Wembley_panorama_3.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="2139" data-file-height="343" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_panorama_3.jpg" title="File:Wembley panorama 3.jpg"> </a></div><center>A panorama of Wembley during the half time period of an England game</center></div></div></div>\n<p>During the 2012 Olympic Games Great Britain defeated Brazil in the first women\'s international to take place at the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> On 23 November the England women\'s team played at the stadium for the first time when they lost 3\xe2\x80\x930 to Germany in a friendly.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Tottenham_Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tottenham Hotspur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In the 2016\xe2\x80\x9317 season, <a href="/wiki/Tottenham_Hotspur" class="mw-redirect" title="Tottenham Hotspur">Tottenham Hotspur</a> staged four "home" European fixtures in both the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">UEFA Champions League</a> and <a href="/wiki/Europa_League" class="mw-redirect" title="Europa League">Europa League</a> competitions. Spurs set a new record attendance for a Champions League home game in England with over 85,000 fans.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> In April 2017 Tottenham confirmed that they had chosen to use Wembley Stadium for all their home fixtures in the <a href="/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_Tottenham_Hotspur_F.C._season" title="2017\xe2\x80\x9318 Tottenham Hotspur F.C. season">2017-18 season</a>, this being due to their existing White Hart Lane Stadium being demolished to make way for the club\'s new stadium for which construction work had already commenced.\n</p><p>Tottenham also used Wembley for their first four home Premier League matches and all home matches from the group stage of the Champions League in 2018\xe2\x80\x9319.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_league">Rugby league</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Rugby league">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_(23rd_August_2014)_003.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG/220px-Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG/330px-Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG/440px-Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_%2823rd_August_2014%29_003.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teams_lining_up_before_the_2014_Challenge_Cup_Final_(23rd_August_2014)_003.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/Castleford_Tigers" title="Castleford Tigers">Castleford</a> contested the <a href="/wiki/2014_Challenge_Cup" title="2014 Challenge Cup">2014 Challenge Cup final</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> <a href="/wiki/Challenge_Cup" title="Challenge Cup">Challenge Cup</a> Final had been played annually at the old Wembley Stadium since 1929. In 2007, the cup final returned to its traditional home after the rebuilding of Wembley.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> When <a href="/wiki/Catalans_Dragons" title="Catalans Dragons">Catalans Dragons</a> played <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_R.F.C." title="St Helens R.F.C.">St. Helens</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2007_Challenge_Cup_Final" title="2007 Challenge Cup Final">2007 Challenge Cup Final</a>, they became the first non-English rugby league team to play in the final. The result saw St Helens retain the cup by a score of 30\xe2\x80\x938 before 84,241 fans.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> The first rugby league team to win a game at the new Wembley Stadium, were <a href="/wiki/Freeston_Business_and_Enterprise_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Freeston Business and Enterprise College">Normanton Freeston</a>. The <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> secondary school beat <a href="/wiki/Castleford_High_School_Technology_and_Sports_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Castleford High School Technology and Sports College">Castleford High School</a> in the Year 7 boys Carnegie <a href="/wiki/Champion_Schools" title="Champion Schools">Champion Schools</a> final, which was played immediately prior to the 2007 Challenge Cup Final.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> The first official try at the renovated Wembley was scored by <a href="/wiki/James_Roby" title="James Roby">James Roby</a> of St Helens, although Luke Metcalfe of Castleford High School scored the first try in the schools game that took place before the 2007 Challenge Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2011, International rugby league returned to Wembley for the first time since 1997 when <a href="/wiki/Wales_national_rugby_league_team" title="Wales national rugby league team">Wales</a> lost to <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Kiwis" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand Kiwis">New Zealand</a> 0\xe2\x80\x9336<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Australian_Kangaroos" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian Kangaroos">Australia</a> beat host nation <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a> 36\xe2\x80\x9320<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> in the <a href="/wiki/2011_Rugby_League_Four_Nations" title="2011 Rugby League Four Nations">2011 Rugby League Four Nations</a>. The semi-finals of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a> were played at Wembley Stadium where <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">defending champions</a> New Zealand beat England 20\xe2\x80\x9318, and eventual tournament champions Australia defeated <a href="/wiki/Fiji_Bati" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiji Bati">Fiji</a> 64\xe2\x80\x930. The double header drew 67,575 fans to Wembley, the second highest crowd for an international rugby league game at either the original or the new stadium.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" rowspan="2">67,545\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>Semi-final\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b9/Flag_of_Australia.svg/46px-Flag_of_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="640" /></span>\n</td>\n<td>64\xe2\x80\x930\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_league_team" title="Fiji national rugby league team">Fiji</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Fiji.svg/23px-Flag_of_Fiji.svg.png" width="23" height="12" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Fiji.svg/35px-Flag_of_Fiji.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Flag_of_Fiji.svg/46px-Flag_of_Fiji.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></span>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Castleford_Academy" title="Castleford Academy">Castleford Academy</a> (formerly Castleford High School) currently hold the record for the most Rugby League appearances at the New Wembley Stadium. On 24 August 2013 their Year 7 Rugby team played RGS High Wycombe in the annual schools curtain-raiser to the Challenge Cup final.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> This was Castleford Academy\'s 4th appearance at the stadium since 2007. This puts them joint with <a href="/wiki/Leeds_Rhinos" title="Leeds Rhinos">Leeds</a> and one appearance ahead of <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Wolves" title="Warrington Wolves">Warrington</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union">Rugby union</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Rugby union">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg/220px-%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg/330px-%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg/440px-%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:%22Wemberley.......Wemberley%22_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1770078.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Wembley in rugby union formation, with posts up before <a href="/wiki/Saracens_F.C." title="Saracens F.C.">Saracens</a> played <a href="/wiki/Worcester_Warriors" title="Worcester Warriors">Worcester Warriors</a> in 2010.</div></div></div>\n<p>The first top level <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> match was a non-cap match between the <a href="/wiki/Barbarian_F.C." title="Barbarian F.C.">Barbarians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Australia national rugby union team">Australia</a> on 3 December 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Between 2009 and 2017. The stadium was used regularly by <a href="/wiki/Saracens_FC" class="mw-redirect" title="Saracens FC">Saracens</a> for some major <a href="/wiki/Aviva_Premiership" class="mw-redirect" title="Aviva Premiership">Aviva Premiership</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heineken_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Heineken Cup">Heineken Cup</a> and International matches. Their Aviva Premiership clash with <a href="/wiki/Harlequin_F.C." title="Harlequin F.C.">Harlequins</a> in 2012 was played before a crowd of 83,761, a world record for a rugby union club match. In 2014, the teams faced again in front of 83,889 spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The 2015 match between Saracens and Harlequins had a new world record attendance for a club game of rugby union with 84,068.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The stadium was also used during the <a href="/wiki/2015_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2015 Rugby World Cup">2015 Rugby World Cup</a>, during which it hosted two pool matches:\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" Zealand</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg/23px-Flag_of_New_Zealand.svg.png" width="23" height="12" title="Argentina national rugby union team">Argentina</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" style="text-align:center;">89,019<sup id="cite_ref-rwc_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rwc-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>27 September\n</td>\n<td>Pool D Match\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Ireland</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="800" /></span>\n</td>\n<td>44\xe2\x80\x9310\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Romania_national_rugby_union_team" title="Romania national rugby union team">Romania</a><span class="flagicon">&#160;<img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/23px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/35px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Flag_of_Romania.svg/45px-Flag_of_Romania.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></span>\n</td>\n<td style="text-align:center;">89,267<sup id="cite_ref-rwc2_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rwc2-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The 89,019 crowd for the New Zealand versus Argentina game set a new record attendance for a Rugby World Cup game.<sup id="cite_ref-rwc_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rwc-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> The Ireland versus Romania match one week later improved this record again to 89,267.<sup id="cite_ref-rwc2_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rwc2-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Although the 90,000 seat Wembley was the largest stadium used during the 2015 Rugby World Cup, the World Cup Final was held at the 82,000 seat <a href="/wiki/Twickenham_Stadium" title="Twickenham Stadium">Twickenham Stadium</a>, the traditional home of the tournament\'s host, England\'s <a href="/wiki/Rugby_Football_Union" title="Rugby Football Union">Rugby Football Union</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_football">American football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: American football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NFL_International_Series" title="NFL International Series">NFL International Series</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg/220px-NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg/330px-NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg/440px-NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NFL_International_Series_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Build up to the <a href="/wiki/NFL_International_Series#2010" title="NFL International Series">2010</a> game between <a href="/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a></div></div></div>\n<p>On 28 October 2007, in front of 81,176 fans, the <a href="/wiki/2007_New_York_Giants_season" title="2007 New York Giants season">New York Giants</a> defeated the <a href="/wiki/2007_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="2007 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a> by a score of 13\xe2\x80\x9310 in the first <a href="/wiki/NFL_regular_season" title="NFL regular season">regular season</a> <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> game ever to be played in Europe, and the first outside of North America.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The first touchdown scored at Wembley was on a run by Giants\' quarterback <a href="/wiki/Eli_Manning" title="Eli Manning">Eli Manning</a>. The NFL have hosted at least one regular season game a year at Wembley since.\n</p><p>On 21 August 2012, the <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> announced a four-year deal to become temporary tenants of Wembley by playing one regular season game each year between 2013 and 2016 and becoming the first team to return to Wembley in consecutive years.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 16 October 2012, the NFL announced there were to be two NFL regular season games played at Wembley Stadium during the 2013 season. The <a href="/wiki/2013_Pittsburgh_Steelers_season" title="2013 Pittsburgh Steelers season">Pittsburgh Steelers</a> at <a href="/wiki/2013_Minnesota_Vikings_season" title="2013 Minnesota Vikings season">Minnesota Vikings</a> on 29 September 2013 and the <a href="/wiki/2013_San_Francisco_49ers_season" title="2013 San Francisco 49ers season">San Francisco 49ers</a> at <a href="/wiki/2013_Jacksonville_Jaguars_season" title="2013 Jacksonville Jaguars season">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> on 27 October 2013. This is an attempt by the NFL to strengthen the NFL fanbase in London and internationally. Future plans to have a permanent NFL team in London have been suggested.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another first was recorded in 2014 as three regular season NFL games were played at Wembley. The <a href="/wiki/2014_Oakland_Raiders_season" title="2014 Oakland Raiders season">Oakland Raiders</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="2014 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a> on 28 September at 6&#160;pm BST, the <a href="/wiki/2014_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2014 Atlanta Falcons season">Atlanta Falcons</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_Detroit_Lions_season" title="2014 Detroit Lions season">Detroit Lions</a> on 26 October at 1:30&#160;pm GMT and the <a href="/wiki/2014_Jacksonville_Jaguars_season" title="2014 Jacksonville Jaguars season">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> hosted the <a href="/wiki/2014_Dallas_Cowboys_season" title="2014 Dallas Cowboys season">Dallas Cowboys</a> on 9 November at 6&#160;pm GMT.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> At 9:30&#160;am ET, the Detroit-Atlanta game was the earliest kick off in NFL history and gave fans a unique four game window on this day.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> In 2015, another first occurred as the first ever divisional match took place at Wembley between the <a href="/wiki/2015_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="2015 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a> and <a href="/wiki/2015_New_York_Jets_season" title="2015 New York Jets season">New York Jets</a>.\n</p><p>On 30 October 2016, for the first time in an NFL game played outside the US, the game carried into overtime and subsequently ended in a tie (another first for both Wembley and a <a href="/wiki/NFL_International_Series" title="NFL International Series">London Game</a>) in a week 8 match between the <a href="/wiki/2016_Washington_Redskins_season" title="2016 Washington Redskins season">Washington Redskins</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2016_Cincinnati_Bengals_season" title="2016 Cincinnati Bengals season">Cincinnati Bengals</a>. The final score was 27\xe2\x80\x9327.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boxing">Boxing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Boxing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 31 May 2014, Wembley Stadium hosted its first boxing event, featuring <a href="/wiki/Carl_Froch_vs._George_Groves_II" title="Carl Froch vs. George Groves II">the rematch between Carl Froch and George Groves</a> for the <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Federation" title="International Boxing Federation">IBF</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Association" title="World Boxing Association">WBA</a> <a href="/wiki/Super-middleweight" class="mw-redirect" title="Super-middleweight">super-middleweight</a> titles.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The contest was held in front of a crowd of 80,000 spectators, a British post-war attendance record for a boxing event, surpassing the crowd at the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Manchester_Stadium" title="City of Manchester Stadium">City of Manchester Stadium</a> when it hosted <a href="/wiki/Ricky_Hatton_vs._Juan_Lazcano" title="Ricky Hatton vs. Juan Lazcano">Ricky Hatton vs. Juan Lazcano</a> in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Boxing_Association" title="World Boxing Association">World Boxing Association</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Boxing_Federation" title="International Boxing Federation">International Boxing Federation</a> heavyweight championship <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Joshua_vs._Wladimir_Klitschko" title="Anthony Joshua vs. Wladimir Klitschko">fight</a> between <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Joshua" title="Anthony Joshua">Anthony Joshua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wladimir_Klitschko" title="Wladimir Klitschko">Wladimir Klitschko</a> broke the attendance record on 29 April 2017, with an attendance of approximately 90,000.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_connections">Transport connections</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Transport connections">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The stadium is described as a "public transport destination"<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> for which parking is available on a very limited basis. To alleviate the impact of vehicular traffic on the local residents and businesses, <a href="/wiki/Brent_Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Brent Council">Brent Council</a> have introduced a number of measures in relation to on street parking and to access restrictions of roads that surround the stadium.\n</p><p>The "Wembley Stadium Protective Parking Scheme" sets a boundary in which parking on street is restricted to only those that hold an event day parking permit. Road closures are in force from 10:00&#160;am on the event day until midnight and apply to Fulton Road, Engineers Way and South Way.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wembley_Stadium_map.png/220px-Wembley_Stadium_map.png" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wembley_Stadium_map.png/330px-Wembley_Stadium_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Wembley_Stadium_map.png/440px-Wembley_Stadium_map.png 2x" data-file-width="1141" data-file-height="867" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wembley_Stadium_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map of Wembley Stadium in relation to <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Way" title="Olympic Way">Olympic Way</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Central_station" title="Wembley Central station">Wembley Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_railway_station" title="Wembley Stadium railway station">Wembley Stadium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Park_tube_station" title="Wembley Park tube station">Wembley Park</a> stations, and the <a href="/wiki/A406_road" class="mw-redirect" title="A406 road">A406 North Circular Road</a> (bottom right)</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail_and_Underground">Rail and Underground</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Rail and Underground">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The stadium is connected to two <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">London Underground</a> stations: <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Park_tube_station" title="Wembley Park tube station">Wembley Park Station</a> (on the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_line" title="Metropolitan line">Metropolitan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jubilee_line" title="Jubilee line">Jubilee</a> lines) via <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Way" title="Olympic Way">Olympic Way</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Central_station" title="Wembley Central station">Wembley Central</a> (<a href="/wiki/Bakerloo_line" title="Bakerloo line">Bakerloo line</a>) via the <a href="/wiki/White_Horse_Bridge" title="White Horse Bridge">White Horse Bridge</a>. Rail links are provided at <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Central_station" title="Wembley Central station">Wembley Central</a> (<a href="/wiki/London_Overground" title="London Overground">London Overground</a>, <a href="/wiki/Southern_(train_operating_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern (train operating company)">Southern</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_Midland" title="London Midland">London Midland</a> services) and <a href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_railway_station" title="Wembley Stadium railway station">Wembley Stadium railway station</a> (<a href="/wiki/Chiltern_Railways" title="Chiltern Railways">Chiltern Railways</a> services).\n</p><p>Stations near by:\n</p>\n<table class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cmglee_London_Wembley_aerial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view of Wembley Stadium and its surroundings</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Onsite_parking">Onsite parking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Wembley_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Onsite parking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The onsite parking facility is shared with Wembley Arena, essentially being the open air surface parking surrounding the eastern flank of Wembley Stadium and the <a href="/wiki/Multi-storey_car_park" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-storey car park">multi-storey car park</a>. These are called Green Car Park and Red Car Park, respectively. There is disabled parking available onsite, at the Green Car Park, at a reduced rate but on a first come first served basis. On some football event dates, opposing team supporters have been separated into the two different car parks.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
